I do draft my wife into trimming the neck-line--again using the Cruzer but this time without the guide.<br /><br />So, I like it, I'm using it to cut my hair.   98. Over the years, I must have purchased about 10 beard/mustache trimmers. None were perfect, and all were overpriced. Either the rechargeable batteries died after a year or two, the blades didn't cut well, the attachments were poorly designed, or they were cheaply made overall. Given the fact that there are so few of these units on the market, one has no choice but to conclude that most men either do not have facial hair, or don't demand higher-quality trimmers -- if they did, the companies that make them would need to produce better units. Well, I finally found one that I like -- this Braun has the qualities that I was looking for in a single package. The unit is well-made and well-designed, the motor is strong, the blades are high-quality, the comb attachments are well-designed and easy to remove, the attachment length adjustment setting locks into place and won't accidentally move, the battery holds a decent charge, and it isn't overpriced. This unit comes with 2 comb attachments, each for a different range of lengths. The markings aren't some arbitrary scale, but in mm of hair length. The blades are sharp and high-quality, and can be immersed in water for cleaning. The unit comes with oil to keep the blades lubricated. The locking mechanism for the attachments cannot accidentally move while in use, which is a problem with a lot of other trimmers. The detail trimmer works really well, and allows you to see what you are doing while using it. The unit comes with a decent travel pouch, and the charger is a cable that plugs into the unit, which I like better than being a transformer that it sits in while plugged into the wall -- requiring outlet space which you may not have. It doesn't have a vacuum for the hair clippings, and the main blade cannot be easily removed for cleaning, as it pivots on a hinge, but these are minor criticisms given its ease of use and build quality. I used this for the first time yesterday, and am pleased with the job it did as well as the trimmer itself. Recommended.

  105. Braun makes top flight personal care products and this one is no different, you can tell the moment you pick it up that it is a cut above the rest. I used to do a lot of comparison shopping with products of this type, but Braun has gotten so good that I simply do a price check or might briefly look at the competition, then I buy the top of the line Braun product every time.... this, the 790 shaver, they all are actually worth the extra money, which is something you can't often say about electrics purchases. The Cruzer 6 Trimmer is the top of the line trimmer product above the Cruzer 5 and has a bit better construction and comb accessories than the 5. It also has some kind of 'dual battery' construction which I don't know a lot about. Points of interest - Battery lasts a very long time and shines above other trimmers of this type by a mile.. there are complaints on line about it not being replaceable, but my experience is that sealed unit batteries perform so much better than replaceable that I much prefer sealed unit. - the battery and cutting performance is so good that it's actually feasible to replace a 120v hair cutter like a Wahl full size with this.... I was very surprised by this, but it's true. - it's very quiet for this type of trimmer and has a very low buzz - when using the bare blade without the comb, the tip has been finished so that it won't scratch / scrape your skin, it's very comfortable to cut in hairline on the back of neck etc. and feels smooth when used this way, much better than the rest. - it is a little smaller and lighter than I expected from the picture, which is good as it's very maneuverable etc. but it is still big enough to do large areas quickly. - there are two comb accessories, a long and a short each adjustable to 6 increments measured in mm. The short is the most useful and adjusts to 1,3,5,7,9, and 11mm length. There are release buttons on both sides to completely remove the comb to use as a straight trimmer or put theother comb on for different lengths. - the trimmer is very effective and cuts through thick hair very easily... so much so that (while I didn't try to do so) I could imagine giving and actual all over haircut with it. There's definitely enough battery endurance to do that, it cuts like a champ, and the long comb goes to lengths for tight military haircuts and even a little longer. - a very minor gripe is that the depth adjustment button can be accidentally pressed during use if you hold it in an unusual way, so there is a slight possibility of shearing off an eyebrow if you are a freak about the way you hold it ;) - one hint: the curvature of the tip casts a little doubt as to what side of it you put towards the skin, you should look inside the comb to verify which way to hold it until you get used to using it I mistakenly dropped it about 5 feet onto ceramic tile about an hour after I opened it (of course) and it came through like a champ.... so I genuinely have nothing negative to say about it enjoy.

  174. Much like you are doing right now, I poured over hundreds of reviews on numerous trimmers before I settled on one. I chose the Braun 6 Head and Beard trimmer and am very satisfied with my choice. Short review: Lightweight, Low vibrations, Low noise, cuts very well, short charge time, attached retractable small/narrow trimmer, can trim while plugged in, and covers a wide hair length range. The price is very good compared to how nice and versatile this trimmer is. Originally I was looking for a more affordable item, but the reviews urged me to spend a little more. Very thick, longer hair will clog up the trimmer quickly, so removing the comb and dumping the hair is required. It's a minor inconvenience at best. Definate recommend. Long review: When I read reviews, I read the bad ones first. Most of them said the same thing and they were far outweighed by the positive reviews. I trim/shave most of the regions on my body, and I will cover each area at a time. First, the trimmers are very lightweight which is nice when trimming your head with lifted arms for an extended periods of time. Compared to most other trimmers (especially plug in versions) the vibration and noise are nominal. The body is plastic and half of it is rubberized for improved grip. The trimmer fits well in your hand and is laid out very well. Unlike the Braun 5, the Braun 6 has a shorter charge time once you perform the initial charge. The indicator light does a great job of letting you know the state of your charge as well, both charging and discharging. My body hair ranges from very coarse and wirey, to very thin and light. I did not have one single hair pull/snag. The hardest part of using the trimmer is figuring out what length setting to use! The trim length guide is clearly marked and will not jump out of the setting. There are two detachable combs. One gives you lengths from 1 to 10 millimeters, and the other gives you from 10 to 20 millimeters. Not using a comb at all will give you a very close to the skin trim. The Braun 6 also has a retractable, narrow-head secondary trimmer. This smaller trimmer is great for reaching small and narrow areas, such as under the nose and around the top of the ears, among others. The comb prongs, although they are plastic, are pretty stiff and keep skin out, and hair cuts level with very little comb bending or deflection. As with most plastic appliances, you should take care to not be rough with the trimmer, the combs particularly. A reasonable level of care will yield many years of use out of this trimmer. I dropped mine from a four foot shelf after its first use, and it still works just fine (whew!). The trimmer comes with a small travel case and the charger has a curled cord so it doesnt tangle up if you are trimming while plugged in. I tested using the trimmer while plugged in with a very low battery. It ran at full strength, which is a very nice feature instead of having to wait for the charge. Charge time for the Braun 6 is 1 hour. My sessions are between 30-40 minutes and it was still running strong at the end. Goatee: My facial hair is very thick, coarse, and wire-like! The Braun 6 cut it all quickly with ease. My facial hair curls a little and some of those can be tricky to get all one length, so I recommend using a fine tooth comb to get the hair as straight as possible for an even cut. Head hair: My hair up top is very thick and straight. I wear a military 'high and tight' hair style. The trimmer cuts very quickly and efficiently. It took only a couple passes to get everything even and at the proper length. The only fault I found is that thick hair will clog up the area between the blades and the comb. I did need to stop every several passes to remove the comb and dump the hair clump. It only did this on the longer hair on top of my head, not the sides or elsewhere on my body. The advantage is that I could dump the hair clumps where I wanted instead of it going everywhere, like with regular clippers. Chest hair: My chest hair is fairly wirey. Once again, no issues with cutting here. Pubic region: Let's face it, tons of people trim that area and will do so with these clippers. Pubic hair is normally fairly coarse and curly,as is mine. Even on extremely soft and delicate skin, there were no dreaded hair snags. Also, the comb prongs do a very good job of preventing skin from making contact with the cutting blades. Of course you should always trim with caution down there to prevent unwanted contact, especially on skin that folds easily. The small size of the trimmer makes reaching certain areas very easy and less awkward. I know that when I get home from overseas, my wife will steal this trimmer and use it for her trimming! Underarms: My underarm hair is very light and thin. This was the only area that I had some difficulty getting an even cut. Due to the hair being so light, it didn't want to be guided into the comb prongs and into the blades. If you have hair like this over larger areas, you may need to make many passes to get a good, even cut. As you can tell, I am pleased with my purchase. The only unknown now is long-term life span. If I can get 2 years out of this trimmer, I will feel as if I got my money's worth. I have no reason to believe the trimmer won't go well beyond that time frame.

I purchased the Braun Cruzer 6 because I wanted the best possible product to maintain and shape the &#34;chin strap&#34; type of beard that I had going. Hindsight is 20/20, so if you're looking for anything that fits the description of what I was looking for, take heed to this review and don't make the same mistake that I did.<br /><br />At first it seemed that the product was sufficient, although I immediately noticed that it wasn't providing the precise trimming that I was looking for. I figured the little extension precision trimmer would meet my needs in the detailing department, but it did not. In fact, it would've been less painful dry-shaving against the grain with a straight-edge razor. I understand that it was marketed as a beard and head trimmer first and foremost, but the description made it sound as though it was the best of both worlds. Unfortunately, this razor isn't the &#34;best&#34; of anything. In fact, that word doesn't even exist in the world that the Cruzer 6 exists in. I've been rather civil up to this point, but now I'm going to reveal the way this excuse for a razor has made me feel inside.<br /><br />I'm going to make this easy for you. The world is full of many extremely diverse and unique people whose needs and preferences vary greatly. So I'm going to list the potential reasons that one would want to purchase this item.<br /><br />Buy a Braun Cruzer 6 Beard & Head Trimmer if:<br /><br />- You absolutely love charging electric razors. If nothing excites you more than constantly having to plug your charger into the<br /> wall, this is the one for you!<br /><br />- You enjoy the feeling of small metal serrations tugging at your hair when you try shaping your beard and ripping it off your face.<br /><br />- You want an electric razor that contains a precision-trimming extension whose sole purpose in life is to painfully rip hair from your<br /> face.<br /><br />- You want a razor that loses it's ability to trim hair within a year of owning it. Even if you apply lubricating oil, the Cruzer 6 won't let<br /> you down!<br /><br />This review may seem nothing more than a biased submission from a disgruntled owner, but I have learned all of these facts the hard way. I maintained my Cruzer 6 perfectly and it still looks the way it did when I first removed it from the box (Oh the expectations that were so soon to be dissolving in failure). The precision extension never really did much since day 1. But after maybe a year of owning it, it has been rendered useless to me. I've tried using different angles, flipping sides...it doesn't matter. No matter how you apply it to the hair you wish to trim, it grips it and rips it. From reading the product description, I thought for sure the battery life was going to be a great quality. Not so much. Nay, not at all. It can be left on the charger until it reaches full capacity, chances are, within the next two times (if not the very next time) you go to use it, you'll be greeted by a nice little flashing red light. If you don't plug your razor back into the wall immediately after you're done using it and leave it to charge, you're gonna have a bad time.<br /><br />This concludes my review of the Braun Cruzer 6. I'm not a newbie to shaving who doesn't know how to maintain a razor. I was in the Marine Corps for over 4 years where I shaved every day of my life. I've tried the expensive electric razors like the &#34;Pulsonic&#34; that supposedly provides a skin-close shave, I've used disposable razors, safety razors, straight-edged razors, water-less shaving gel, expensive shaving creams...So this wasn't my first rodeo. I don't normally leave reviews on anything I buy, but when something makes me unusually upset and disappointed in, I create a review to (1) seek justice against the product that betrayed me, and (2) make it public so others will hopefully not purchase it and learn the hard way like myself. However, if this razor does sound like the one for you, then have at it. Because I assure you, everything I've listed here WILL happen. And if that's the case, I have a Braun Cruzer 6 in great shape for sale.

It has a good ergonomic feel, although if you've used different devices it may take a little time to get acclimated to the positions of the power and hair comb length settings. The unique design places the hair length settings on the removable comb itself, not the body of the trimmer. This greatly reduces problems with inadvertently changing that setting when the comb is removed to do edging around the beard and mustache. Since there are two hair comb attachments provided, people who frequently use two settings can even set oneon each. Although absolutely unimportant to me, I will concede that the attachments look sort of cool the way they appear to float over the cutter head. Overall, this product does everything I want very well, specific to the task of beards and mustaches. The packaging is embarrassing, with the normally classy Braun choosing to try and market this trimmer to what I can only imagine they call the \\"urban youth\\" market. Fonts are in a fake graffiti style, and cartoon faces depict the types of grooming you can do with it (\\"You can make yourself look like a pirate!!\\"). Doesn't really seem geared toward adults.<br /><br />For $40 I'd expect a Li-Ion battery, and maybe even self-sharpening (or at least maintenance free) blades. Instead you've got NiMH cells, and in the travel case included for the trimmer (a nice touch... the case is actually pretty solid) is a small bottle of mineral oil to keep the blades oiled.<br /><br />Being waterproof is cool, but I don't have a mirror in my shower and I'm never going to shave in there, so I don't know what that's really worth.<br /><br />The \\"precision trimmer\\" seems all but worthless. To start with, it's designed confusingly with the button to extend it looking like it's where the power button should be (got me the first few times I used this Braun). If you have the long hair trimmer on the shaver it doesn't even extend out beyond it, making it unusable. If you have the normal (1-10mm) attachment on it just barely sticks out, and you can't really see it so I don't know how you're supposed to trim with any real precision.<br /><br />The first time I used this trimmer it took me many passes to trim down my beard. The guides seemed too rigid, and with large spaces between the teeth that made me nervous about getting an even shave around the contours of my face (actually, the spacing on the blades themselves seem pretty far apart aswell). The longest 10mm setting of the beard attachment seems just slightly above stubble length to me, and is definitely not meant for those of us who want to maintain a full beard. Somewhat related, the \\"hair\\" attachment which allows for longer length trimming isn't well suited for use on the face.<br /><br />--<br /><br />Wrap up:<br /><br />I'm sure this is fine for many (read: those who just want to keep well groomed stubble), but I've come to expect more of Braun and was let down by this product with the price point it is sold at ($40.19 as of March, 2014). I think I would have been happier spending ten dollars more to get something like the [[ASIN:B003U8ESI4 Philips Norelco QT4070 Vacuum Trimmer]] (which can go up to 18mm, has li-ion battery AND a vacuum!), or spend $10 less to get something like the [[ASIN:B005PUZZR8 Remington MB4040 Li-Ion Trimmer]]. It's worth noting that both of these options have blades that don't require oiling like the Braun.

Normally I would chalk this up as a more powerful cutting motor, but it sure doesn't help it cut.<br />Also the charging cord has is cumbersome. Rather than the little transformer being in the unit, ala the Remington, or a small box, ala many small electronics, the Braun has this huge plug that juts out maybe 4 or 5 inches straight out from the outlet. I'm not saying it's a hazard or even that you could knock it out of the outlet easier (which you could), but it just looks stupid and good luck trying to plug that thing in an outlet behind a dresser, bed, end table, etc.<br /><br />Upshot:<br />The areas that the Baruan Cruzer 6 compares favorably to my present Remington MB-200 Titanium are largely cosmetic and pale in comparison in the areas that it fails at. Take away all the other knocks and you'd still have the fact that it DOES NOT cut well. That's really the only thing you need to know.sically failed at it's primary job - cutting. Obviously goatee trimming isn't comparable to head hair trimming, but in my mind I would think that cutting your hair with a trimmer like this would be HARDER than any other application and if can't handle my somewhat thin/short goatee, I'm not confident that it can handle anything else.<br />Another thing I didn't like is it vibrated much more in my hand than the Remington. It really annoys me that they didn't bother with this.<br /><br />So, to summarize: It's a pretty good trimmer; but if you buy one, please be super careful never to overcharge it. In fact if you stay within one range of lengths (either 1mm to 11mm or 10mm to 20mm) you never have to change anything<br /><br />Cons:<br />- The guard (the thing with the teeth that allows you to adjust the hair length) clogs easily when using it on my head. I'm nearly bald on top and my hair's not thick elsewhere so there's no reason for that. It helps when I trim my hair every week but I'd rather go 2 weeks between trims.<br />- I need to redo the same spots many times in order to get an even trim.You'd figure 2 or maybe 3 passes would be enough but it feels like 10 in some places<br />- I've yet to find a use for the little detail trimmer. Its placement makes it awkward to use.<br /><br />So to summarize: It works well enough that I didn't feel the need to send it back but I can't give it an unreserved recommendation.
